Drought Relief
(Question No. 5026)
Mr Kerin asked the Minister for Primary Industry, upon notice, on 8 September 1982:
( I) Has he announced a drought relief package for primary producers.
(2) Does that include a subsidy on interest rates over 12 per cent.
(3) Will that policy be administered through the trading banks.
(4) How will primary producers who use vendor finance Obtain that subsidy.
Mr Nixon-The answer to the honourable member's question is as follows:
(I) Yes. On 31 August 1982 I announced two drought relief initiatives which will be directly funded by the Commonwealth. They are a subsidy on fodder purchased to feed drought affected sheep and cattle and a subsidy on interest payments at rates of interest higher than 12 per cent on debt incurred by drought affected farmers. Details of both schemes were elaborated in information papers I issued with a Media Release on 24 September 1982.
(2) Yes. See answer to (I) above.
(3) No. The interest rate subsidy scheme will be administered by a special administration unit located in the Commonwealth Department of Primary Industry. The fodder subsidy scheme will be administered by the authority in each State responsible for administering the National Drought Relief Arrangements.
(4) Subject to other eligibility criteria all formal debts including vendor finance will qualify for the interest subsidy.
Department of Veterans' Affairs: Reorganisation ofCentral Office
(Question No. 5103)
Mr Holding asked the Minister representing the Minister for Veterans' Affairs, upon notice, on 16 September 1982:
(I) What was the reason for the reorganisation of the top structure of the central office of the Department of Veterans' Affairs which 'was approved by the Public Service Board in May 1982.
(2) When was the review commenced which led to this reorganisation.
(3) Who were the (a) Departmental and (b) other Public Service officers who carried out the review.
(4) Who initiated the review, and when.
(5) Who was responsible for submitting the review report and its recommendations to the Public Service Board.
(6) What problems and deficiencies were identified by the review.
(7) Will the Minister present the review report to Parliament; if not. why not.
(8) How many officers at (a) the central office and (b) regional offices, will be attached to the Benefits and Special

Projects Division which has been approved by the Public Service Board.
(9) What is the designation, classification and salary of each of those officers.
(10) How many ofthose officers will be personnel who are currently employed in the Vietnam Special Studies Group.
Mr Thomson-The Minister for Veterans' Affairs has supplied the following answer to the honourable member's question:
(I) to (10) The top structure of the Department's Central Office had remained basically unchanged since 1964. The main purpose of the review was to examine the current and future roles of the Divisions, analyse any problems and deficiencies with the structure and provide a more efficient, upgraded organisation, better suited to our needs.
The review was initiated by the Permanent Head in November 1981 and preliminary work, fact finding, et cetera, commenced from that time.
The Permanent Head submitted the final report to the Public Service Board.
The review was conducted as an internal, departmental organisation review and was submitted for the Public Service Board to handle under section 29 of the Public Service Act. This is consistent with the approach adopted in such reviews. Information about the re-organisation was provided to Senate Estimates Committee 'G' on 16 September 1982.
So far only the top structure (Second Division) part of the Benefits and Special Projects Division has been approved by the Public Service Board. Three positions are involved in this part of the Division. The remainder of the organisation currently includes 32 positions but this may change when the rest of the organisation review is completed. There are no officers in Branch or Regional Offices attached directly to the Benefits and Special Projects Division. Since the re-organisation has not been completed, information about who will occupy various positions cannot be provided.

Nuclear Accidents: Insurance
(Question No. 450 I)
Mr Les Johnson asked the Treasurer, upon notice, on 28 April 1982:

(I) Are nuclear exclusion clauses cQI'I\ained in property

and liability insurance policies such that, in the event of any

accident with nuclear materials involving damage or contami-

nation, insured property owners would; be, unable to claim

compensation.

': I;'

(2) If so, what is the attitude of the CIl,lTImOnwealth in the
case of such eventualities with regard tathe acceptance of liability.

(3) By what process can householders residing in close proximity to the Lucas Heights Atomic Research Establish-
ment, NSW, indemnify themselves against the possibility of incurring losses sustained as a result of a mishap at that establishment.

Mr Howard-The answer to the honourable member's question is as follows:

(I) I understand from inquiries made' of the insurance industry by my officers that it has been established practice for many years for property and liability policies issued by insurance companies in Australia to provide for a number of general exclusions which exclude cover, inter alia, in respect of risks as a consequence of war, invasion; acts of foreign enemies, hostilities (whether war be declared or not) and any loss attributable to nuclear weapons material, nuclear fuel or nuclear waste from nuclear fuel. While an insured person could not claim under his insurance policy in respect of nuclear damage that falls within an exclusion clause, it could be open to such a person to claim compensation under common' law from the person or persons responsible for the damage sustained.

(2) The attitude of the Commonwealth with regard to acceptance of liability would depend largely on whether the Commonwealth itself was responsible for the damage sustained. As indicated in part (2) of my answer to House of Representatives Question No. 3676 (Hansard) of 18 August 1982, page 650), whether the Commonwealth would be liable to meet any loss resulting from nuclear damage would depend on the facts of each particular case. Broadly, where the Commonwealth uses radioactive materials or is directly responsible for their use, any Commonwealth liability would depend on general principles of liability that would apply equally to private persons or corporations.

(3) It is my understanding that insurance is not available from the insurance industry in Australia to cove,r householders against any loss sustained as a result of a mishap at the Australian Atomic Energy Commission establishment at
Lucas Heights and that it would be a matter for a householder to claim compensation at common law. The Commonwealth would, of course, stand by the Commission to ensure its ability to meet any damages awarded against it. However, the Commission maintains the highest standards of safety of its nuclear
facilities and the Government believes that the possibility of accidents arising out of the Commission's operations at L!lcas Heights is highly unlikely. My comments in (2) above are also relevant. As indicated in my answer to Question No. 3676, certain reviews ,are in process in this area as a result of Commonwealth action and consideration is being given, inter alia, to the adequacy 'of the protection afforded under common law, to persons who sustain loss or damage arising from the use of nuclear material.

Nutrition and Diet
(Question No. 4971)
Mr Humphreys asked the Minister for Health, upon notice, on 25 August 1982:
(1) Has his attention been drawn to a statement by the Australian Association of Dieticians which claimed that the Australian public was being fed misleading and often untrue information on nutrition and diet.
(2) Is that statement correct, if so, what is his Department doing to co-ordinate a nutrition education program in the public and private sectors
Mr CarIton-The answer to the honourable member's question is as follows:
(1) Yes.
(2) It is my Department's view that the statement is substantially correct. My Department has undertaken nutrition education activities in both the public and private sectors for many years.
A wide range of nutrition education publications is produced by my Department and by the National Health and Medical Research Council (NH and MRC). These publications provide both a reference for the development of nutrition education and an authoritative source of scientifically based information on food and nutrition for the public. They are widely distributed and include booklets and pamphlets such as Eat Better for Less, Dietary Guidelines for Australians, Nutrition Messages for the Ethnic Community, Welcome to Meals on Wheels, Your Health and Your Figure, Tables of Composition of Australian Foods, Simplified Food Composition Tables and Dietary Allowances for Use in Australia, as well as the poster A Food Guide for Good Health.
Officers of my Department co-operate with industry, including primary producer groups and commodity boards and food manufacturers, in the development of nutrition education programs.
In 198 I my Department sponsored a National Nutrition Education Conference, at the recommendation of the NH and MRC which brought together representatives of the State and Territory health authorities and nutrition and educational bodies. At its Ninety-second Session in October 198 I, the NH and MRC acted on one of the Conference recommendations in approving the establishment of a sub-committee of the Council to consider such matters as the co-ordination of nutrition education activities on a national basis. The subcommittee is expected to hold its first meeting later this year.

Defence Capacity: Effect of Closure of Foundries
(Question No. 5004)
Mr Holding asked the Minister for Defence Support, upon notice, on 7 September 1982:
(I) Has his attention been drawn to allegations made by companies which constitute part of the Australian foundry industry that a large number of foundries have been closed as a result of the uncontrolled importation, or dumping, of castings into Australia and that such closure of foundries could severely affect the defence capacity of Australia.
(2) Has he caused any inquiries to be made to (a) examine the relationship between the foundry industry and Australia's defence needs and (b) examine the allegations made concerning the problems of the industry; if so, what inquiries, and what conclusions has he reached.
Mr Viner-The answer to the honourable member's question as follows:

(I) A check has been made of records of dumping complaints received by the Department of Industry and Commerce over the last 12 months. In relation to castings there have been three complaints lodged which are identified as possibly falling within this category. They concern railway wheels from Japan and Korea, manhole covers from India and Singapore, malleable cast iron pipe fittings from Japan.
(2) The general capabilities of the foundry industry are monitored on a continuing basis. Foundries which form part of the defence industry base are reviewed at least annually and departmental records of their defence capabilities are adjusted accordingly.
Although the foundry industry is an important element of the defence industry base, defence requirements, especially in time of peace, represent only a small percentage of the industry's total capacity.
Considerable support has been provided to the foundry industry in recent years in relation to defence work and a number of specialised development tasks have been funded, including valves for naval fire extinguishing systems; submarine snorkel and hull valves; large propellor shaft supports and other ferrous items for the RAN FFG class frigates; aluminium bronze propellors for the FFG frigates; high strength diecastings for sonobuoys.
In summary, although the increased competition and general downturn being experienced by Australian foundries is a matter of concern to the Department of Defence Support, specific recent allegations of dumping do not appear to be directly related to its defence production function. Areas of the industry having special defence significance are closely monitored and are continuing to receive support.
Recommendations by the Committee of Review of Commonwealth Functions: Department of Aboriginal Affairs
(Question No. 5005)
Mr Holding asked the Minister for Aboriginal Affairs, upon notice, on 7 September 1982:
(I) Have he and his Department, over the course of the last 3 years, received representations from community based Aboriginal organisations for an examination of wages and conditions of employees of these organisations.
(2) Have these representations sought increases in salary levels and improvement in conditions.
(3) Is he able to say whether (a) there has been no real adjustment to the salaries or wages of employees of Aboriginal organisations since 1976, as alleged by members of these organisations, and (b) there has been no attempt to implement a superannuation scheme or to guarantee permanency.
Mr Wilson-The answer to the honourable member's question is as follows:
(I) Yes.
(2) In a number of cases, yes.
("3) (a) In determining the level of grants to Aboriginal organisations, it is my Department's normal practice to relate salary and wage rates for funded positions to existing awards or to similar positions in the public or private sectors where this is possible. Grants have been increased to cover increases in the salaries and wages paid to employees of Aboriginal organisations.

2486 REPRESENTATIVES 21 October 1982

Answers to Questions

(b) Permanency and other conditions of employment are matters for consideration by individual Aboriginal organisations. As a general principle, only contributions to the Commonwealth Superannuation Scheme may be funded by the Commonwealth. Community-based Aboriginal organisations do not come within the definition of an 'approved authority' under the Superannuation Act 1976 and their employees are therefore not eligible to contribute to the Commonwealth Superannuation Scheme. It is a matter for consideration by individual organisations whether they negotiate superannuation packages for their employees.
